CRITICISM OF VON WALDEBSEE
to meet Its obligations with respect to in
demnity. This proposal contemplates the
appointment of an international board of
financiers which shall periodically collect
from China the amount of money which
foreign Ministers in Peking say she can
pay, and this sum shall be distributed
among the powers In proportion to the
value of bonds issued to them by the Chi
nese Government.
Should the Chinese Government fail to
pay the amount the board fixes upon after
consultation with the foreign Ministers
as reasonable, then each power shall lose
in proportion to the amount of bonds it
has received. Individual action is to be
prohibited and the seizure of territory Is
not to occur in case China shall fail to
make payment. ,'
Special Commissioner Rockhill, who has
communicated the information regarding
this proposal to the State Department, has
been carefully instructed by the State De
partment as to the attiude of he President
thereon. Rockhill's instructions permit
his acceptance of the general features of
the proposal.
Whether the powers would be willing to
adopt the plan outlined cannot be said at*
this time, as some of the Ministers in Pe
king are as yet without Instructions from
their Governments. Even should the plan
fall of adoption, however, it is the purpose
of the administration to insert in the ttnal
treaty to be entered into a provision for
the establishment of the "open door". 1 and
if possible a provision insuring the integ
rity of China. The question of the method
to be adopted to obtain payment of the
indemnity cannot be determined until the
amount of indemnity is fixed, and the
State Department is still insisting that
there should be a substantial reduction.

TACOMA, May- 21.â Mrs. Chajles Gun
zert, wife of a plumber, to-day shot and
killed her 13-year-old son and then com
mitted suicide by taking carbolic acid
The tragedy occurred in the woods west
of Lake Park station and was .evidently
premeditated, as the mother had invited
the boy out for. a walk.
The revolver, a three-ounce bottle of
carbolic acid arid a bottle of strychnine
were, carried by the desperate woman.
The boy was shot four times in the back
and side. Mrs. Gunzert's face was pressed
close to that of her sonâ so close, in fact,
that the. carbolic acid running out of her
mouth-fell upon and burned the fleshon
the boy's- cheek. . The bodies were found
ehortly after the. tragedy by a man wan
dering through the woods.
Mrs. Gunzert was the daughter of John
H. Anderson, a prominent politician. Her
physician says she was mentally . unbal
anced for some time.

The escape of the passengers from the
wrecked â¢ train was almost miraculous.
The train was struck by a. wall of water
fourteen feet high and carried down with
the bridge. The passengers, eighteen In
number, succeeded in reaching places of

BOSTON, Mav 21.â Former Congressman
Charles A.' Boutelle of Bangor, Me., died
to-day at the McLean Asylum, Waverly,
where he had been confined . for a ,year
with brain trouble. â¢ Death was due'.pri
marily to pneumonia.- which developed
last Sunday. Boutelle's daughter, Grace,
who has been at the head of the house
hold since her mother's death in 1832, was
at the bedside to-day. . . .
Boutellei was 62 years . old, and on. his
retirement from. Congress Jast winter
was placed on the retired list of the navy
as a captain, an office to which he was
eligible by reason of his Civil War and
Congressional committee services. Three
daughters survive him. .
Boutelle's illness dated from December
21, 1S99, when he was seized by a~ fit ' of
unconsciousness "while at a hotel In this

WEST POINTERS
AWIT DISGRACE
Five Cadets Will Be Dis
missed From the
Academy.
War Department Shows No
Mercy to Recalcitrant
. Students.
Special Dispatch to Tne Call. : ' ~
CALL BUREAU, 1406 G STREET. N.
W.. WASHINGTON, May 21.â LitUe
mercy was shown to-day to cadets at
the Military Academy found by the court
of Inquiry convened by Colonel Mills, the
superintendent, to be guilty of Insubor
dination. Five were dismissed, six were
suspended and half a hundred were or
dered deprived of their privileges. Cadets
Stephen B. Vernon of New York and
Charles S. Perry of Iowa will be dis
missed In accordance with the findings of
a court-martial. â¢
WEST POINT. May 21.â Deep gloom
pervaded the cadet corps when the un
official information reached here regard
ing the disciplinary measures. - Colonel
Mills will return from Washington to
morrow, bringing with him the official or
ders. He will cause five men to be notified
of their dismissal by noon, thus prevent
ing them from reporting for afternoon
and evening duty at 2 o'clock, the usual
time. At dress parade, a few minutes
after 6 o'clock, as the corps is assembled
on the grounds, the cadet adjutant will
read out the sentences, including, besides
the five dismissed, six men suspended.
The expulsion of five cadets at one time
for disciplinary reasons is without parallel
In the history of the academy. The au
thorities regret the necessity far such
drastic action, but they feel that it is an
essential to the well-being of the acad
emy. Of course the cadets are said to
have been implicated in the demonstra
tion against Colonel Mills. Five were ac
cused of conceiving and leading it, twen
ty-five of actual participation and eighty
three were declared to be partlceps crlm
inis, in that they aided and abetted the
deed by encouraging shouts, and cheers.
The five chief offenders accused are re
ceiving the most severe penalty. Only
six of the second-class offenders are being
punished now, leaving nineteen of those
thus accused to be tried.

of tho commercial department of the uni

subject was "The Commercial Age."

A. Bates and Kintaro Migasaki, San Jose.

conferred upon Harold Tuttle.

GOLDEN JUBILEE
OF UNIVERSITY
yÂ«N AKLAND, May 2Lâ The retire
fi \\ ment of George Estes, chairman
II JJ of the Southern Pacific system
division of the Order of Railway
Telegraphers, and B. A. Myers,
secretary of the division, was not volun
tary, though resignations prepared by the
two are now on their way to Grand Presi
dent Dolphin at St. Louis. Before the res
ignations arrived Grand President
Dolphin removed both of the Pacific Coast
officials. The actual reason for the dif
ferences between Estes and Dolphin Is
the refusal of the Order of Railway Teleg
ruphers to recognize the new general or
der of railway men known as the United
Brotherhood of Railway Employes.
Estes possesses great ability as an_or;
gauizer, and has taken much interest in.
tho organization of the new general order
of railroad employes. This was not pleas
ing to the officers of the Order of Rail
way Telegraphers, and a few weeks ago
â¢Dolphin himself made a trip to San Fran
cisco to look into this very matter. He
returned to the headquarters of the order
in St. Louis without taking any action,
and the removal of Estes was of recent
date.
A dispatch from St. Louis, sent out
through the regular news channels of the
Associated Press, tells the story of the
removal of Estes and Myers without
mentioning their names. This dispatch
rends:
President M. M. Dolohln of the Order of Rail
way Telegraphers, â¢aho has just returned to the
headquarters of that organization from a busi
ness trip through the East, when shown a dis
patch statins that the Order of Railway Teleg
raphers is interested in the establishment of an
organization similar to the old American Rail
way Union on the Pacific Coast, said:
"The Order of Railway Telegraphers Is
neither officially nor otherwise connected with
euch a movement. It is true that two of our
local officials in San- Francisco were connected
with the movement, and they were removed
from office by me a few days ago on that ac
count. The plan of organizing all railway em
ployes into one organization is not feasible, and
it is my belief that it never will be. The old
class organizations which are now in .-exist
ence and have been for years have accom
plished great good for the railway employes,
and there is no reason why they cannot con
tinue to do so. I will reiterate that we have
not only not aided or abetted this new move
ment, but that we have not recognized It in
any way."
This is a plain statement coming
from the head of one of the strongest of
the railway orders. Taken together with
the announced removal of Estes and
Myers, It means that as far as the officials
of the Orders of Railway Telegraphers
are concerned they will not recognize the
new general railway order.
Estes has thrown himself bodily into tho
new order, and it remains to be seen
whether he can get the telegraphers into
It or whether the officers of the Order of
Railway Telegraphers can hold them to
the old organization. .
This will be an important railroad ques
tion, for the telegraphers are now very
Btrong. particularly on the Southern Pa
cific Company's system. Between San
Francisco and Portland on the north,
Stockholders of the Cramp , Company
will, it is said, have the option of taking
cash or exchanging 1 their holdings, share
for share, for a 7 per cent preferred stock
in the new company. There is $a.000,000
worth of Cramp stock and $15,000,003 cash
will be necessary to buy out Bethlehem..
PHILADELPHIA, May 21.â The Press

houre only.

Iron Company stock at about the present
market price of C3.

New York syndicate, which is to under
write the present combination, has been
compelled to raise about 515,000,000 In act
ual cash, as it is entirely a money trans
action, and fully that much will be re
quired to purchase the two Bethlehem
companies' stock. It will take $7,000,000 to
buy the Bethlehem steel stock.

OLD SOAKERS.
Get Saturated With. Caffeine.
When a person has used coffee for a
number of years and gradually declined
Jn health, it is time the coffee should be
left off In order to see Â¦whether or. not
that has been the cause of the trouble.
A lady in Huntsville, Ala., Mrs. S. M.
IJrazler, cays she used coffee for about
40 years, and for the past 20 years was
troubled with stomach trouble. "I have
been treated by many physicians, but all
in vain. Everything failed to perfect a
cure. Was prostrated for some time and
came near dying. When I recovered suf-
ficiently to partake of food and drink I
tried coffee again and it soured on my
stomach.
I finally concluded coffee was the cause
of ray troubles and stopped using' it. I
tried tea and then milk In its place, but
neither agreed with me, then I com-
menced using Postum Food Coffee. I
had it properly made and it was very
pleasing to the taste.
I have now used It four months and
my health is so greatly improved that I
can eat almost anything I want and can
Bleep well, whereas, tefore, I suffered for
years with Insomnia,
I have found. the cause of my troubles
and a way to get rid of them. You can
depend upon It I appreciate Postum."

COMMERCIAL NEWS
breeder of AneTora, . goats, has Just re
ceived four Angora goats from Turkey,
which have been procured to replenish
his herds. This is the first importation
of Angora - goats from Turkey to the
United States in twenty-seven years. The
Turkish Government prohibits the expor
tation of goats, and the animals had to be
smuggled out of the country.

Smugglers to Obtain the
Animals.

Situation in Oakland.
OAKEAND,- May 21.â The machinists'
strike situation in Oakland is unchanged
to-day. Each side Is awaiting such moves
as may- be made in San Francisco, the
results - here practically depending upon
action across the bay. The molders and
coremakers were at -work to-day in the
shops, -and cannot strike unless orders
come from the Eastern headquarters. Un
ion pickets have been placed on duty at
the works affected. \ There will be no
places filled at the various works for, the
present at least. The employers are hope
ful that. a compromise may be reached,
although there is every indication that the
molders will Join the machinists. In that
event the several works will be compelled
to shut down. *V-
All houses who sign an agreement to
patronize only manufacturers who abide
by the rules of the association will be
furnished with union cards, which they
will be requested to display in a conspicu
ous place. The officers of the association
consist of I* ..Van Laak of the "Van Laak
Manufacturing Company, president, and
J. P. Henry of the California Broom Man
ufacturing Company, secretary and treas
urer. The companies comprising the asso
ciation are the Van 'Laak Manufacturing
Company, the California Broom Manufac
turing Company, Taylor Bros, and Zan
Bros. & Co. /
The broom makers of this city held a
meeting last night at 201S Howard street
and permanently organized themselves
into Â¦ a union under the name of the Cali
fornia Broom Manufacturers' Association
for protection against Chinese labor and
the prison labor of other States. By-laws
were adopted pledging the members of
the association not to deal with any mer
chant, wholesale or retail, who carried in
his stock goods not bearing the label of
the International Broom Makers' Union.
The broom makers were also bound not
to patronize or to employ Chinese 'under
any circumstances.

The regular weekly meeting of the Bar
bers' Union was held -Monday night at
Laurel Hall, Shiels building, 102 O'FarreU
street. The attendance was, as usual,
good. Secretary Currier's report showed
a healthy financial condition of the union.
There is in the hands of the trustees $1000,
with more to be added from the proceeds
of the late picnic. Â¦ The present member
ship has exceeded the 1000 mark/ with sev
eral applications in the hands of the in
vestigating committee to be acted upon.
No positive action Was taken regarding
the machinists' strike other than the pass
ing of a resolution of sympathy," but all
affiliated ;unions are given to understand
that the Barbers' Union will cheerfully
respond in aid' of those out on strike
should it be called upon to render assist
ance.

STEADY GROWTH
OF COMPANIONS
Interesting Report of the
Grand Chief of the
Order.
Nine Circles "Were Instituted
and Two Suspended
Last Year.
The Rrand officers and delegates to the
Grand Circle of the Companions of the
Forest. A. O. F., went out on a trolley
ride yesterday morning and did not return
until late, consequently there was but a
short session in the afternoon.
A resolution was adopted granting to
social members who became - such prior
to May, 1S90, the right to funeral benefits
the same as beneficial members.
The grand organist was by. vote added
to the executive board. . " " Â»
A vote of thanks was passed to Max
Boehm past grand chief companion, for
many sen-ices rendered to the order. Â¦
Grand Chief Mrs. M. E. Falconer In her.
report says: â¢_ :
It affords me much pleasure to report that
our order has done fairly well during the past
year. As a rule harmony has reipned through
out our Jurisdiction. As In my pervious term.
I have not hesitated to enforce "order and
decorum" whenever I deemed It necessary for
the best interests of our beloved order. In
three Instances I found it necessary to
use the "weedinsr out process" with exce.Ient
results, getting rid of an element among
whom "discord and strife" was omnipresent.
In Franklin Circle No. 115 one offending
member was brought before the board of final
arbitrators and by a. verdict of said board ex
pelled from this order. Â¦ â ' -
In Pride of the Forest Circle No. 122 I found
much discord and detailed a special deputy for
the circle, under whose guidance the circle
has become harmonious and prosperous.
In Loyal Circle No. 1T9 I found It necessary
to suspend the circle, reinstate the law-abiding
members and bring the offending ones to trial
before the final arbitrators, all of whom have
been duly expelled, and Loyal Circle is now
less Jn membership, but Infinitely ricner In
peace, hannony and fraternity.
With the exception of these Instances the
order is in thorough concord and hannony.
During the past year S69 candidates were
lr.Jtlated as members of this order. Nine new
circles were instituted and two were sus
pended, and 604 members were either suspended
or expelled, leaving a net gain of over 265
members and seven circles for the year ending
March SI. 1901: 125 members have been ini
tiated since that date, making a total gain
From the reports of the supreme secretary
3-cu will eee that the funds of our subordinate
circle e have increased in a satisfactory man
ner, and that our financial standing Improves
m each year rolls by. At our previous^ cession
the total funds ot our various circles amounted
to the sum of-rrS10 6S; at this time the total
funds amount to J896S 67, showing an increase
of J11R7 99 for the year.
Durlne the past term fourteen claims have
been paid from this fund. Its management
and benefits have given entire satisfaction
throughout the order and I see no necessity
for any change in its laws.
In the evening the grand officers, dele
gates and members of the order enjoyed
a night at the Central Theater.
To-day the election for grand officers
will take place.
EXPRESSMAN WOLF TO
LOSE HIS PROPERTY
Sis Horses and "Wagron Seized . for
Confiscation and Sale Under
the I/aw.
J. W. Wolf, the aped expressman who
was acquitted last Monday of the charge
of smuggling a trunk containing opium
into Mrs. Tapley's lodging-house. 217
Stockton street, is a victim of circum
stances and although undoubtedly inno
cent will be likely to lose his two-horse
team and wagon.
' His accuittal on the criminal charge
does not tret him out of his troubles, for.
under the provisions of the United States
statutes on the subject of smuggling,
United States District Attorney Wood
worth will be obliged to institute, civil
proceedings for the confiscation Â«->f the
team and wagon. The guilt or innocence
of the owner of the ship or other vehicle
in which smuggled goods are transported
is not material to the issue, the law pro
viding that such vehicles shall be seized
and sold for the benefit of the Govern
ment. While his horses and wagon are
in the custody of the Federal ofllcials
Wolf is deprived of his only means of
support. In ord*>r to relieve the old man's
necessity Mr. Woodworth has consented
to ask the Secretary of the Treasury to
allow Mr. Wolf to rive bonds and use
his team and wagon until the confiscation
proceedings shall have been ended.
